Rust comes with a variety of things in its standard library. However, if\\n4: //! you had to manually import every single thing that you used, it would be\\n5: //! very verbose. But importing a lot of things that a program never uses isn't\\n6: //! good either. A balance needs to be struck.\\n7: //!\\n8: //! The *prelude* is the list of things that Rust automatically imports into\\n9: //! every Rust program. It's kept as small as possible, and is focused on\\n10: //! things, particularly traits, which are used in almost every single Rust\\n11: //! program.\\n12: //!\\n13: //! # Other preludes\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Preludes can be seen as a pattern to make using multiple types more\\n16: //! convenient. As such, you'll find other preludes in the standard library,\\n17: //! such as [`std::io::prelude`]. Various libraries in the Rust ecosystem may\\n18: //! also define their own preludes.\\n19: //!\\n20: //! [`std::io::prelude`]: crate::io::prelude\\n21: //!\\n22: //! The difference between 'the prelude' and these other preludes is that they\\n23: //! are not automatically `use`'d, and must be imported manually. This is still\\n24: //! easier than importing all of their constituent components.\\n25: //!\\n26: //! # Prelude contents\\n27: //!\\n28: //! The items included in the prelude depend on the edition of the crate.\\n29: //! The first version of the prelude is used in Rust 2015 and Rust 2018,\\n30: //! and lives in [`std::prelude::v1`].\\n31: //! [`std::prelude::rust_2015`] and [`std::prelude::rust_2018`] re-export this prelude.\\n32: //! It re-exports the following:\\n33: //!\\n34: //! * <code>[std::marker]::{[Copy], [Send], [Sized], [Sync], [Unpin]}</code>,\\n35: //!   marker traits that indicate fundamental properties of types.\\n36: //! * <code>[std::ops]::{[Fn], [FnMut], [FnOnce]}</code>, and their analogous\\n37: //!   async traits, <code>[std::ops]::{[AsyncFn], [AsyncFnMut], [AsyncFnOnce]}</code>.\\n38: //! * <code>[std::ops]::[Drop]</code>, for implementing destructors.\\n39: //! * <code>[std::mem]::[drop]</code>, a convenience function for explicitly\\n40: //!   dropping a value.\\n41: //! * <code>[std::mem]::{[size_of], [size_of_val]}</code>, to get the size of\\n42: //!   a type or value.\\n43: //! * <code>[std::mem]::{[align_of], [align_of_val]}</code>, to get the\\n44: //!   alignment of a type or value.\\n45: //! * <code>[std::boxed]::[Box]</code>, a way to allocate values on the heap.\\n46: //! * <code>[std::borrow]::[ToOwned]</code>, the conversion trait that defines\\n47: //!   [`to_owned`], the generic method for creating an owned type from a\\n48: //!   borrowed type.\\n49: //! * <code>[std::clone]::[Clone]</code>, the ubiquitous trait that defines\\n50: //!   [`clone`][Clone::clone], the method for producing a copy of a value.\\n51: //! * <code>[std::cmp]::{[PartialEq], [PartialOrd], [Eq], [Ord]}</code>, the\\n52: //!   comparison traits, which implement the comparison operators and are often\\n53: //!   seen in trait bounds.\\n54: //! * <code>[std::convert]::{[AsRef], [AsMut], [Into], [From]}</code>, generic\\n55: //!   conversions, used by savvy API authors to create overloaded methods.\\n56: //! * <code>[std::default]::[Default]</code>, types that have default values.\\n57: //! * <code>[std::iter]::{[Iterator], [Extend], [IntoIterator], [DoubleEndedIterator], [ExactSizeIterator]}</code>,\\n58: //!   iterators of various\\n59: //!   kinds.\\n60: //! * <code>[std::option]::[Option]::{[self][Option], [Some], [None]}</code>, a\\n61: //!   type which expresses the presence or absence of a value. This type is so\\n62: //!   commonly used, its variants are also exported.\\n63: //! * <code>[std::result]::[Result]::{[self][Result], [Ok], [Err]}</code>, a type\\n64: //!   for functions that may succeed or fail. Like [`Option`], its variants are\\n65: //!   exported as well.\\n66: //! * <code>[std::string]::{[String], [ToString]}</code>, heap-allocated strings.\\n67: //! * <code>[std::vec]::[Vec]</code>, a growable, heap-allocated vector.\\n68: //!\\n69: //! The prelude used in Rust 2021, [`std::prelude::rust_2021`], includes all of the above,\\n70: //! and in addition re-exports:\\n71: //!\\n72: //! * <code>[std::convert]::{[TryFrom], [TryInto]}</code>.\\n73: //! * <code>[std::iter]::[FromIterator]</code>.\\n74: //!\\n75: //! The prelude used in Rust 2024, [`std::prelude::rust_2024`], includes all of the above,\\n76: //! and in addition re-exports:\\n77: //!\\n78: //! * <code>[std::future]::{[Future], [IntoFuture]}</code>.\\n79: //!\\n80: //! The first version of the prelude is used in Rust 2015 and Rust 2018,\n30: //! and lives in [`std::prelude::v1`].\n31: //! [`std::prelude::rust_2015`] and [`std::prelude::rust_2018`] re-export this prelude.\n32: //! It re-exports the following:\n33: //!\n34: //! * <code>[std::marker]::{[Copy], [Send], [Sized], [Sync], [Unpin]}</code>,\n35: //!   marker traits that indicate fundamental properties of types.\n36: //! * <code>[std::ops]::{[Fn], [FnMut], [FnOnce]}</code>, and their analogous\n37: //!   async traits, <code>[std::ops]::{[AsyncFn], [AsyncFnMut], [AsyncFnOnce]}</code>.\n38: //! * <code>[std::ops]::[Drop]</code>, for implementing destructors.\n39: //! * <code>[std::mem]::[drop]</code>, a convenience function for explicitly\n40: //!   dropping a value.\n41: //! * <code>[std::mem]::{[size_of], [size_of_val]}</code>, to get the size of\n42: //!   a type or value.\n43: //! * <code>[std::mem]::{[align_of], [align_of_val]}</code>, to get the\n44: //!   alignment of a type or value.\n45: //! * <code>[std::boxed]::[Box]</code>, a way to allocate values on the heap.\n46: //! * <code>[std::borrow]::[ToOwned]</code>, the conversion trait that defines\n47: //!   [`to_owned`], the generic method for creating an owned type from a\n48: //!   borrowed type.\n49: //! * <code>[std::clone]::[Clone]</code>, the ubiquitous trait that defines\n50: //!   [`clone`][Clone::clone], the method for producing a copy of a value.\n51: //! * <code>[std::cmp]::{[PartialEq], [PartialOrd], [Eq], [Ord]}</code>, the\n52: //!   comparison traits, which implement the comparison operators and are often\n53: //!   seen in trait bounds.\n54: //! * <code>[std::convert]::{[AsRef], [AsMut], [Into], [From]}</code>, generic\n55: //!   conversions, used by savvy API authors to create overloaded methods.\n56: //! * <code>[std::default]::[Default]</code>, types that have default values.\n57: //! * <code>[std::iter]::{[Iterator], [Extend], [IntoIterator], [DoubleEndedIterator], [ExactSizeIterator]}</code>,\n58: //!   iterators of various\n59: //!   kinds.\n60: //! * <code>[std::option]::[Option]::{[self][Option], [Some], [None]}</code>, a\n61: //!   type which expresses the presence or absence of a value. This type is so\n62: //!   commonly used, its variants are also exported.\n63: //! * <code>[std::result]::[Result]::{[self][Result], [Ok], [Err]}</code>, a type\n64: //!   for functions that may succeed or fail. Like [`Option`], its variants are\n65: //!   exported as well.\n66: //! * <code>[std::string]::{[String], [ToString]}</code>, heap-allocated strings.\n67: //! * <code>[std::vec]::[Vec]</code>, a growable, heap-allocated vector.\n68: //!\n69: //! The prelude used in Rust 2021, [`std::prelude::rust_2021`], includes all of the above,\n70: //! and in addition re-exports:\n71: //!\n72: //! * <code>[std::convert]::{[TryFrom], [TryInto]}</code>.\n73: //! * <code>[std::iter]::[FromIterator]</code>.\n74: //!\n75: //! The prelude used in Rust 2024, [`std::prelude::rust_2024`], includes all of the above,\n76: //! and in addition re-exports:\n77: //!\n78: //! * <code>[std::future]::{[Future], [IntoFuture]}</code>.\n79: //!\n80: //! [std::borrow]: crate::borrow\n81: //! [std::boxed]: crate::boxed\n82: //! [std::clone]: crate::clone\n83: //! [std::cmp]: crate::cmp\n84: //! [std::convert]: crate::convert\n85: //! [std::default]: crate::default\n86: //! [std::future]: crate::future\n87: //! [std::iter]: crate::iter\n88: //! [std::marker]: crate::marker\n89: //! [std::mem]: crate::mem\n90: //! handling, prelude v1 vs edition-specific module exports, and resolver behavior changes between edition 2018 and 2021 span the following key files:\\n\\n## Standard Library Prelude Modules\\n\\n### library/core/src/prelude/mod.rs\\nDefines all edition-specific prelude modules: `rust_2015`, `rust_2018`, `rust_2021`, `rust_2024`, and `rust_future`. The `rust_2015` and `rust_2018` modules simply re-export `super::v1::*`. The `rust_2021` module additionally adds `crate::iter::FromIterator` and `crate::convert::{TryFrom, TryInto}` — the key trait additions that change behavior between edition 2018 and 2021.\\n\\n### library/core/src/prelude/v1.rs\\nThe base v1 prelude, re-exported by both `rust_2015` and `rust_2018`. Contains marker traits, ops traits, and basic collection/conversion traits, but NOT `TryFrom`, `TryInto`, or `FromIterator`.\\n\\n### library/std/src/prelude/mod.rs\\nThe std-layer edition-specific preludes: `rust_2015` and `rust_2018` re-export `super::v1::*` only; `rust_2021` additionally re-exports `core::prelude::rust_2021::*` (which adds `TryFrom`, `TryInto`, `FromIterator`).\\n\\n### library/std/src/prelude/v1.rs\\nThe std base v1 prelude, including built-in macros, standard types, and re-exports from `core::prelude::v1`.\\n\\n## Compiler: Injection of Edition-Specific Preludes\\n\\n### compiler/rustc_builtin_macros/src/standard_library_imports.rs\\nThe `inject()` function inserts the edition-specific prelude import at the beginning of every crate. Key behaviors:\\n- Emits `#[macro_use] extern crate std` with `ident_span = span` (def-site hygiene) for edition >= 2018, but `call_site` for 2015 — this controls macro_use hygiene between editions.\\n- Selects the edition-appropriate prelude path: `Edition2015 => sym::rust_2015`, `Edition2018 => sym::rust_2018`, `Edition2021 => sym::rust_2021`, etc.\\n- In 2015, the import path is absolute with a leading `::` (PathRoot); in 2018+ it is not.\\n\\n## Compiler: Resolver Behavior Changes\\n\\n### compiler/rustc_resolve/src/lib.rs\\nDefines the `macro_use_prelude` field (`FxIndexMap<Symbol, NameBinding>`) populated by `#[macro_use]` extern crates. Also defines `ModuleOrUniformRoot::ExternPrelude` (used for `::foo` paths in edition 2018+) and `ModuleAndExternPrelude` (for `::foo` from 2015 edition macros used in 2018+ crates).\\n\\n### compiler/rustc_resolve/src/ident.rs\\nCore name resolution with the most edition-specific branching:\\n- `kw::PathRoot` + `ident.span.at_least_rust_2018()` resolves to `ExternPrelude` (2018+ behavior: `::foo` refers to external crates)\\n- `kw::PathRoot` + `ident.span.is_rust_2015()` + session at_least_rust_2018 → uses `ModuleAndExternPrelude` (cross-edition macro hygiene for 2015-edition macros in 2018+ crates)\\n- `Scope::MacroUsePrelude` searches `macro_use_prelude` for macros imported via `#[macro_use]`\\n- Edition 2015 flag (`rust_2015`) controls macro scope ordering\\n\\n### compiler/rustc_resolve/src/build_reduced_graph.rs\\nBuilds the reduced module graph. Handles `#[macro_use]` on extern crates (adding macros to `macro_use_prelude`). Enforces that in 2018+ editions, visibility paths must be crate-relative (via `crate::`) or absolute (`::`) — relative module paths raise `Relative2018` error.\\n\\n### compiler/rustc_resolve/src/diagnostics.rs\\nEdition-specific error messages and suggestions: notes that `TryFrom`, `TryInto`, `FromIterator` are in the prelude starting Edition 2021; explains that `::foo` means extern prelude in 2018+; offers `crate::` prefix suggestions for 2018+ edition.\\n\\n### compiler/rustc_resolve/src/macros.rs\\nMacro name resolution, including scope ordering where prelude macros (from `macro_use_prelude` and std prelude) are searched after `macro_rules!` scopes.\\n\\n## Compiler: Prelude Collision Lints (2018->2021 migration)\\n\\n### compiler/rustc_hir_typeck/src/method/prelude_edition_lints.rs\\nImplements `lint_edition_dependent_dot_call()`: warns when a method call (e.g., `.try_into()`) will become ambiguous in Rust 2021 because `TryInto` is newly added to the prelude. Emits `RUST_2021_PRELUDE_COLLISIONS` or `RUST_2024_PRELUDE_COLLISIONS`.\\n\\n### compiler/rustc_hir_typeck/src/method/suggest.rs\\nMethod resolution suggestions include notes about `TryInto`/`TryFrom`/`FromIterator` being added to the prelude in Edition 2021.\\n\\n### compiler/rustc_lint_defs/src/builtin.rs\\nDeclares the `rust_2021_prelude_collisions` and `rust_2024_prelude_collisions` lints with `FutureIncompatibleInfo` tied to their respective editions.\\n\\n## Edition Abstraction\\n\\n### compiler/rustc_span/src/edition.rs\\nThe `Edition` enum (`Edition2015`, `Edition2018`, `Edition2021`, `Edition2024`, `EditionFuture`) with helper methods `is_rust_2015()`, `at_least_rust_2018()`, `at_least_rust_2021()`, `at_least_rust_2024()`.
